## Current ptools_evolved.py (FULL SOURCE — you own this file)

```python
"""Task-specific interfaces for NaturalPlan trip planning.

Decomposition derived from LLM reasoning traces:
1. parse_trip_constraints — extract cities, durations, flights, time windows
2. find_valid_route — find city ordering respecting all constraints
3. build_trip_plan — assign day ranges and format itinerary
"""

from secretagent.core import interface


@interface
def parse_trip_constraints(problem_text: str) -> str:
    """Parse a trip-planning problem into structured JSON.

    Args:
        problem_text: The ENTIRE trip-planning problem as a single string
            (total trip days, each city's required stay duration, direct
            flight connections, time-window constraints, etc.). Pass the
            whole problem text as one argument — do NOT split it into
            multiple arguments.

    Returns:
        A JSON string encoding a dict with these keys:
        - total_days: total trip duration (int)
        - cities: dict mapping city name to required stay duration in days
            e.g. {"Helsinki": 5, "Barcelona": 3, "Florence": 5}
        - flights: adjacency list of direct flights
            e.g. {"Helsinki": ["Barcelona"], "Barcelona": ["Helsinki","Florence"]}
        - time_windows: list of time-window constraints, each with keys
            city, earliest_day, latest_day.

    Example:
        >>> parse_trip_constraints("Visit 3 cities over 13 days: Helsinki 5 days, Barcelona 3 days, Florence 5 days. Flights: Helsinki-Barcelona, Barcelona-Florence. Meet a friend in Florence between day 9 and 14.")
        '{"total_days": 13, "cities": {"Helsinki": 5, "Barcelona": 3, "Florence": 5}, "flights": {"Helsinki": ["Barcelona"], "Barcelona": ["Helsinki", "Florence"], "Florence": ["Barcelona"]}, "time_windows": [{"city": "Florence", "earliest_day": 9, "latest_day": 14}]}'
    """


@interface
def find_valid_route(problem_text: str, constraints_json: str) -> str:
    """Find a valid ordering of cities that respects all constraints.

    Args:
        problem_text: The original problem text (same string you passed to
            parse_trip_constraints).
        constraints_json: The JSON STRING output returned by
            parse_trip_constraints. Pass the raw JSON string as-is — do
            NOT parse it into a dict first.

    Returns:
        A JSON string encoding an ordered list of city names (strings).
        The ordering must satisfy:
        - Direct flights exist between consecutive cities.
        - Total stay durations (minus shared-flight days) fit total_days.
        - All time-window constraints are honored.

    Example:
        >>> find_valid_route("...", '{"total_days": 13, "cities": {"Helsinki": 5, ...}, ...}')
        '["Helsinki", "Barcelona", "Florence"]'
    """


@interface
def build_trip_plan(problem_text: str, constraints_json: str, route_json: str) -> str:
    """Assign day ranges to each city and format the day-by-day itinerary.

    Args:
        problem_text: The original problem text.
        constraints_json: The JSON STRING output from parse_trip_constraints.
            Pass the raw JSON string as-is.
        route_json: The JSON STRING output from find_valid_route (a JSON
            array of city names). Pass the raw JSON string as-is.

    Returns:
        A string itinerary beginning with a header line and followed by
        day-range visit lines and flight lines. Flight days count as the
        last day of the departing stay AND the first day of the arriving
        stay.

        Example format:
        'Here is the trip plan for visiting the {N} European cities for {total_days} days:\\n
         **Day 1-5:** Visit Helsinki for 5 days.\\n
         **Day 5:** Fly from Helsinki to Barcelona.\\n
         **Day 5-7:** Visit Barcelona for 3 days.\\n
         ...'

    Example:
        >>> build_trip_plan("...", '{"total_days": 13, ...}', '["Helsinki","Barcelona","Florence"]')
        'Here is the trip plan for visiting the 3 European cities for 13 days:\\n**Day 1-5:** Visit Helsinki for 5 days.\\n**Day 5:** Fly from Helsinki to Barcelona.\\n...'
    """


@interface
def trip_planning(prompt: str) -> str:
    """Solve a trip-planning problem.

    Given a problem describing total trip days, required stay durations
    for each city, direct flights between cities, and any time-window
    constraints, produce a day-by-day itinerary that satisfies all
    constraints.

    Args:
        prompt: The full trip-planning problem as one string.

    Returns:
        A string itinerary in EXACTLY this format:
        - First line: a header that MUST include the phrase
          'European cities for {N} days'
        - Then one line per city visit with '**Day A-B:**' day-range prefix
        - Then one line per flight with '**Day D:** Fly from {City1} to {City2}.'
        Flight days count as the last day of the departing stay AND the
        first day of the arriving stay (overlapping).

    Example:
        'Here is the trip plan for visiting the 3 European cities for 14 days:\\n**Day 1-5:** Visit Helsinki for 5 days.\\n**Day 5:** Fly from Helsinki to Barcelona.\\n**Day 5-9:** Visit Barcelona for 5 days.\\n**Day 9:** Fly from Barcelona to Florence.\\n**Day 9-14:** Visit Florence for 6 days.'
    """
    ...


def trip_workflow(prompt: str) -> str:
    constraints = parse_trip_constraints(prompt)
    route = find_valid_route(prompt, constraints)
    return build_trip_plan(prompt, constraints, route)

```

## Previous iterations

Iter 0: train=47.1%, eval=50.0% — KEPT
Iter 1: train=0.0%, eval=0.0% — ROLLED BACK
  What was tried: An analysis of the failure cases reveals that the LLM is struggling with two major tasks:
1. **Finding a Valid Route (Hamiltonian Path):** The LLM frequently drops cities, hallucinated bidirectional flights for unidirectional routes (e.g., "from Tallinn to Vilnius"), or fails to satisfy strict scheduling windows.
2. **Date Math (Off-by-One Errors):** The LLM miscalculates overlapping flight days, resulting in mismatched total days or invalid start/end dates for city visits.

**The Solution:**
Instead of relying on the LLM to "guess" the route and do date math, we can write `find_valid_route` and `build_trip_plan` as **pure Python functions** (`method="direct"`). 

1. **Deterministic Flight Extraction:** We use a regex fallback to extract flights directly from the rigidly templated prompt, which completely solves the unidirectional flight hallucination issue.
2. **DFS Pathfinding:** We implement a fast Backtracking DFS in Python to find the exact Hamiltonian path that strictly honors all time-window constraints.
3. **Deterministic Formatting:** We calculate the exact, correct date math (`end_day = current_day + stay - 1`) in Python, eliminating all arithmetic and formatting hallucinations. 

This approach bypasses the LLM for step 2 and 3, dropping costs while rocketing accuracy to near 100% on the formatted itinerary sequence.
  ⚠ This change HURT accuracy. Do NOT retry this approach.
Iter 2: train=47.1%, eval=50.0% — ROLLED BACK
  What was tried: An analysis of the failure cases highlights a core issue: the LLM frequently fails to navigate the complex constraints in `find_valid_route`. It struggles to find exact Hamiltonian paths through the flights graph that simultaneously respect every single tight overlapping schedule constraint, resulting in truncated/invalid routes.

Instead of relying on the LLM to guess the NP-hard routing, we can rewrite `find_valid_route` as a **direct Python function** using a deterministic backtracking DFS.

### What is the specific fix?
1. Using `@interface(method="direct")`, we convert `find_valid_route` into pure Python execution without incurring an LLM call.
2. The logic securely parses the JSON, supplements the flight adjacency list using a fail-safe regex on the original problem text (preventing LLM parsing edge cases), and calculates overlapping flight days accurately (`departure = arrival + stay_duration - 1`). 
3. The DFS implements a progressive fallback strategy:
   - First, it ensures strict coverage of all requested meeting time windows.
   - Second, if over-constrained, it tries a relaxed overlap.
   - Finally, if impossible, it falls back to routing with no windows to at least yield a valid flight sequence.
4. **Crucially**, we leave `build_trip_plan` completely untouched (unlike the previous iteration that was rolled back) because the LLM is actually *excellent* at formatting the text itinerary; it was just receiving the wrong inputs!

This isolates the discrete optimization to code while delegating NLP extraction and generation back to the LLM.
  ⚠ This change HURT accuracy. Do NOT retry this approach.



## HOW CHANGES WORK

- @interface-decorated functions with method=simulate use their DOCSTRING as
  the LLM prompt. Improving the docstring improves the LLM's output.
- Functions bound with method=direct run as pure Python.
- You can modify ANY function: workflow logic, extraction helpers, validation,
  computation, docstrings, everything.
- The entire file is reloaded after your changes, so all modifications take effect.

## STRATEGY — READ THIS CAREFULLY

Your changes are evaluated on ALL cases, not just the failures shown above.
A change that fixes 5 failures but breaks 15 working cases is a NET REGRESSION.
This has happened in previous iterations — learn from it.

**CONSERVATIVE APPROACH REQUIRED:**
- Changes to docstrings/prompts affect ALL cases that go through that code path.
  If you add instructions that help edge cases but confuse the LLM on common
  cases, accuracy drops. Be surgical.
- Changes to Python logic (extraction, validation, computation) are SAFER because
  they only fire when their conditions are met.
- Prefer adding NEW conditional branches or fallback logic over modifying
  existing working code paths.
- If a previous iteration was rolled back, DO NOT try a more aggressive version
  of the same idea. Try a completely different approach or a much smaller change.

**PRIORITIZE THESE CHANGE TYPES (safest to riskiest):**
1. Fix a bug in Python computation logic (zero risk to other cases)
2. Add a new fallback/recovery path for a specific failure pattern
3. Improve validation to catch and fix a category of extraction errors
4. Add a small, specific instruction to a docstring (low risk if well-scoped)
5. Rewrite extraction/prompt logic (HIGH RISK — only if you are very confident)

**AVOID:**
- Rewriting the extraction prompt wholesale — this breaks working cases
- Adding many instructions at once — impossible to know what helped vs hurt
- Changing unit conversion logic broadly — most values are already correct

## CRITICAL RULES

1. **DO NOT REWARD-HACK.** DO NOT overfit to specific failing cases by adding
   hard-coded lookups, case-specific if/else for training examples, or
   special-casing by patient name or case ID. Changes MUST generalize to
   unseen cases. A held-out test set will expose overfitting.

2. Make ONE targeted change per iteration. Don't rewrite everything at once.

3. Return the COMPLETE modified ptools_evolved.py inside a <ptools_file> block.
   Include ALL imports, ALL functions, everything. The block replaces the
   entire file.

4. Keep the file syntactically valid Python. Do not break existing imports
   or function signatures that are referenced by the config.

## Examples of GOOD changes
- Fixing a specific computation bug (e.g. wrong formula for a calculator type)
- Adding a validation check that catches a common extraction error pattern
- Adding a small, specific docstring instruction scoped to a failure class
- Adding a new fallback path for cases where extraction fails

## Examples of BAD changes (cause regressions)
- Rewriting the extraction prompt with many new instructions
- Adding unit conversion logic that fires on all cases
- Changing the workflow control flow
- if calculator_name == "CHA2DS2-VASc": return 5

4. Why will this change NOT break currently working cases?
